ªÇæ ¡åÇæÄêª¾à ïºå¸à¶Ä¾à ÄÍºå (ºÇæ¸ ¡ÃúÉî¼à Íå ÌÄå°,¡åÚ»ü¨ ÌâÉÚ½¾ ¡ÄåºñºëÄå)(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ¤ÞÛ¯ Ì¶Ç®´ºÇ - ¥Î¿³¼Æ ÁßÁ[´ÆÕÎ¯,±ò¯, Ì¹ÇÝ¿Ç¶Ç¼ ÍººÆ¹Ç´ÆÕ £Îº±Æ±¼Æ)(The Hon. Arumugan Thondaman - Minister of YouthEmpowerment and Socio Economic Development)Ì¯¿¼Á ¼¶È¶Æ ¶±Ç¿¼Æ £Á¼Æ¯Í¿, ¥Þ ¥+ÆÐ ¥¾+ÆÎ¯¶ÆÌ¶ÇÀÈ¾Ç¿¼Æ ¯¶+Æ¯È¼ÙÎ´» ¯´Æ´´¶ÆÎ¶¹Æ ¹½Æ½È» ¬Ý ¼±Æ±ÈÎ¸¯È¿¹Æ¹¹Æ¹´Æ´×° £¶½ÆÐ ·Ç ©ÙÎ´» Í¹±Æ±È ¥Þ¶È¾Æ¹¶È¾¿È¯Æ¯ÈÍ½°Mr. Deputy Chairman, it gives me great pleasure to brieflyoutline some of the more important areas of activities thatmy Ministry is engaged in.

Mr. Deputy Chairman, before proceeding any further,I wish to place on record my appreciation of the gesture ofHis Excellency the President Mahinda Rajapaksa forappointing me as the Minister of Youth Empowerment andSocio Economic Development which is a high profileportfolio providing me considerable responsibility to upliftthe human and socio economic development of the peopleof Sri Lanka, more particularly the youth in the plantations.

I am conscious of the immense potential within myMinistry to address the felt needs of young people who ifleft unattended are the most vulnerable group of thepopulation to fall prey to undesirable elements andpreoccupations.

Mr. Deputy Chairman, it is within the knowledge ofeveryone that I have a special empathy with the hopes,aspirations and the dreams of people in the plantationswhose welfare had been an abiding attachment of my lategrandfather, Savumiamoorthy Thondaman, and myself ofcourse presently.

I was appointed as a Minister in His Excellency’s Cabinetat the end of August this year and since then I have preparedan extensive programme both for the empowerment of youthand for the socio economic development of depressed areasin the country. My Ministry has already held several mobileoffices in depressed areas to collect information for theestablishment of a data base on youth and to understandtheir aspirations. My Ministry will be liaising with severalother Ministries and agencies on implementing training andskills development programmes for youth.

One of the depressed areas that I paid special attentionto is the estate communities, not only because my partyand I represent those communities, but because they are alsorelatively much depressed in comparison with the rest ofthe country.

As you are aware Mr. Deputy Chairman, life is changingrapidly in the estates. Heath indicators have improved inthe past five years due to the work of concerned agenciesin the estate communities and especially due to the workof the Plantation Human Development trust which functionsunder my Ministry. Average education levels are also

2006 ï¾åÉæÂÚ 3021892190

increasing in the estates and as a result expectations arechanging. Furthermore, as technologies such as electricity,mobile phones and computers slowly enter estate life, thedynamics of the estate communities will continue to changeat a rapid pace. Estate communities receive access otinformation and opportunities through these technologicaladvancements. However, new technology needs bo beintegrated into these communities in an equitable andsustainable fashion. Therefore, future investments will haveto accommodate and support incoming appropriatetechnology. The challenge that my Ministry will face duringthe coming years will be to focus more and more on thesocio development of the work and the non-workenvironment of plantation communities.

Accordingly, Mr. Deputy Chairman, my Ministry will,during the next year, address several issues ranging from;estate housing, community infrastructure and services suchas health and sanitation, education and the introduction ofincome supplementation.

My Ministry will Mr. DeputyChairman, pay specialattention to youth and women in developing our strategies.Women who form the backbone of the tea industry, yet asa group constantly exhibit some of the worst healthindicators in the country. The Government as well asmanagement companies should take a keen interest inpreserving women’s health and well-being. For example,improved access to water and firewood, as well as crechesand dispensary services would held to reduce women’sburdens in the estate communities.

At the same time in addressing the aspirations of the youth,my Ministry in association with existing training institutionswill take steps to provide employment-oriented vocationaltraining as well as on-the-job training and work opportunitiesto unemployed youth.

In conclusion, it will be remiss of me if I don not mentionthat programmes, projects and activities identified by myMinistry and made operational are due to the personalcommitments of the staff of the Ministry from the Secretarydownwards to the execuitve and other staff of the PlantationHuman Development Trust and the Thondaman Foundadion.

ÀåÚÈèï¾àºëÉ22592260

[¡. Ãå. 4.14]

ªÇæ ¦. ¦. ¦. ÄêÌàºåÀå ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ©ºÆ° ©ºÆ° ©ºÆ° Û¶¹Ç)(The Hon. M. M. M. Musthaffa)Bismillahir Rahmanir RaheemThank you for the opportunity given to me to speak atthe Committee Stage Discussion on the Votes of the Ministryof Education.

First of all, I would like to commend the Hon. Ministerfor there is no doubt that he has been doing a wonderfuljob of work starting his career from the Provincial Council.Just as the Hon. Hasen Ali mentioned; without any partydifference, without any community difference he has beencontributing impartially towards everybody. So I applaudhim.

Hon. Minister, when the SLEAS, Sri Lanka EducationAdministrative Service was established it was decided thatthe candidates for SLEAS will be selected on the followingcriteria. That is, an open competitive examination - 25per cent, limited competitive examination - 45 per cent andseniority - 30 per cent. But so far SLEAS candidates havenot been selected on that basis. So an injustice has beencaused especially to the Grade I Principals who are actuallyeligible under the seniority category which as I mentionedis 30 per cent.

Sir, on the 1st of March, 2002 Circular 1225/32 revealedthat 1783 SLEAS vacancies have to be filled. So 30 percent from the seniority category have to be recruited. Butwe see that action has been initiated to select people froma limited competitive examination. That is, by anexamination conducted in 2006, whereas the results of theexamination held for the married and the seniority categoryin 2002 have not been released. So they will be affectedand therefore you have to take into consideration thecomplaint of the candidates from the seniority and themarried category. Their exam results have to be releasedbefore the SLEAS selections are made.

The other complaint that I received was from thePresidents of the National Colleges of Education. As youknow, out of the 17 National Colleges of Education youhave only five colleges where you have permanentPresidents. There was an interview conducted on the 3th ofFebruary but the results have not been released nor haveappointments been made. So they feel as if they are drivinga vehicle without a licence and that they have beenperforming the duties as the Presidents of the Colleges ofEducation for the last four or five years without any rewards.

ÄìÈåÌ¾åÇç· Ä¾àºòéºëÄå(¶Î¾Îº¶Ç+ÆÐºÆ §Þ¹Æ¸¼Æ £Á¼Æ¯¿Æ)(The Presiding Member)Hon. Musthaffa, you may continue.

ªÇæ ¦. ¦. ¦. ÄêÌàºåÀå ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ©ºÆ° ©ºÆ° ©ºÆ° Û¶¹Ç)(The Hon. M. M. M. Musthaffa)Now only five Colleges have permanent Presidents. SoAddalaichenai, Batticaloa, Vavuniya, Mahaweli, Uva,Pulathisipura, Aluthgama, Ruwanpura, Sariputhra, Nilwala,Sripada and Jaffna do not have permanent Presidents. Sothe persons covering up this duty feel frustrated anddisappointed for the long delay. Therefore, you have totake into consideration the interview they have faced. Theirresults should be released and appointments made at theearliest.

Now coming to the main point which is regarding theNational Schools and the Provincial Council schools. Thissystem is not moving smoothly, Sir. These National Schoolswere selected on an ad hoc basis. I do not see the basis onwhich those National Schools were selected and there arevery good schools which have all the facilities to getqualified as National Schools. But, you do not have thechance as you are restrained; you are constrained by theWorld Bank that you cannot go ahead and have more andmore National Schools. On the other hand, we know thatwhatever instructions given by you are not properlyimplemented at the provincial level. For example, withregard to the selection of whatever category of teachers. Wehad a tough time in the past appointing volunteer teachers,English teachers and minor employees. The relevantauthorities may have sent out the circular stating the basisadopted in appointing them. But, we do not see any basisbeing adopted at that level. So, what I feel is that the timehas come to abolish this system and bring these schoolsunder one administration. Either you bring the NationalSchools under a provincial administration or bring theprovincial schools up to the level of National Schools. Asit is, you have a lot of problems. Even the problems facedby the school teachers are due to that. I know that. Suppose

2006 ï¾åÉæÂÚ 3022612262

there are just two National Schools in a particulareducational zone, then the transfer could take place onlybetween those two. For example, in Kalmunai, one is aMuslim school and the other is a Tamil school. So, transfersbetween those two schools cannot take place. Even to gettransfers to schools in other provinces is a tedious task. Asyou know, it never takes place. So, the time has come forthe Hon. Minister of Education to take it up at theEducational Reforms Committee. Hon. Minister, you haveto do something.

As you know, teachers are idling in certain schools. Insome schools, there is a need for teachers, but you cannotfind them. This is one of the drawbacks in the system.Especially about the North-East Provincial Council, I donot know what you are going to do. After all, the SupremeCourt judgment was to demerge these two provinces. So,we do not know what will happen. Everything is going todepend on whether you are going to take the North andthe East separately. Anyway, you are going to have a toughproblem.

We see a disparity, a great disparity between the NationalSchools and the provincial schools. Some schools havebeen given the proper facilities: teachers are there; sportsfacilities are there; laboratory facilities are there, everythingis there. On the other hand, you do not find all thesefacilities in other schools. So, the time has come to addressthis issue.

The other thing is that, as you know, we need more andmore technically qualified people for this country. Theprevailing system has to be changed.

ÄìÈåÌ¾åÇç· Ä¾àºòéºëÄå(¶Î¾Îº¶Ç+ÆÐºÆ §Þ¹Æ¸¼Æ £Á¼Æ¯¿Æ)(The Presiding Member)ªÇæ Ä¾àºòéºëÄ¾ø, §ÂºëÄåïªà ¨åÈÆ ¡ÉÌå¾Æú.

ªÇæ ¦. ¦. ¦. ÄêÌàºåÀå ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ©ºÆ° ©ºÆ° ©ºÆ° Û¶¹Ç)(The Hon. M. M. M. Musthaffa)Sir, the change of Chair took one minute. So, you haveto give me that time.

I propose that you have a degree programme for peopleto get technically qualified and also a BSc degree for nurses,which is a gold mine. I mentioned this at the Debate onthe Votes of the Ministry of Labour Relations and ForeignEmployment. You must definitely bring in a BSc degreefor nurses. It is a gold mine. It will bring in a lot of foreignexchange to the country. Next to you, Hon. Minister, yourDeputy Minister, who is also the Deputy Minister ofFinance, is seated there. You will have less problems whenyou improve the foreign employment sector. In additionto that, you should have more nurses training schools,vocational training schools and technical schools becausethere are thousands and thousands of vacancies all over worldand even in the Western countries for technically qualified

people. If you could take necessary action, I am sure theforeign exchange in this country would not be US Dollars2.2 billion, but would multiply by fivefold and become USDollars 10 billion so that you could solve this problem aswell as half of the country’s problems.

Today, the problems are due to the economic disparity. Ifyou can serve the people of this country with equallydistributed economic benefits, there would not be anyproblem; there would not be any ethnic problem in thiscountry. So, basically, education should set the foundationto solve this problem.

Sir, thank you very much for giving me this opportunity.

BOISRI LANKA

BOARD OF INVESTMENT OF SRI LANKAP. O. Box 1768, World Trade Centre - West Tower, EchelonSquare, Colombo 1, Sri Lanka.Date: 22. 11. 2006Our Ref : REC/4/5762/01Your Ref :

Mrs. Malini PeirisAdditional Secretary (Higher Edcation)For SecretaryMinistry of Education - Higher Education Division18, Ward Place,Colombo 07.

Dear Madam,

PROPOSED PRIVATE MEDICAL COLLEGE AT PILIYANDALA

We refer your letter dated 09.11.2006 on the above subject.

Vignan Educational Foundation (Pvt) Ltd was approved by the BOI,in August 2001 to set up a training institution to provide training ininformation technology and para - inedical professionals.

This approval was granted after obraining observations from theMinistry of Higher Education, Ministry of Health and the UniversityGrants Commission (UGC). Ministry of Health had indicated if theinstitution is only for para-medicals that they would recommned theproject but since it involves training medicals undergraduates that theBOI should referred to the Ministry of Higher Education.

As the BOI did not permit the company to undertake pre-clinicalmedical courses, the company filed a case against the BOI and otheragencies demanding that they be permitted to conduct medical courses(pre-clinical).

While hearing of the case was going on, the following boservationfrom government authorities were received.

i)UGC has indicated that the project did not come under itspurview.

ii)Department of Health Services had no objection to theproposal being approved by the BOI subject to registrationbeing obtained from Sri Lanka Medical Council & MedicalCollege Council.

iii)Sri Lanka Medical Council had indicated that the decision ofthe BOI did not depend on the registration of the Council.

Tel: 2385972-6, 2346131-3, 243443-5, 2435027, 2447531Telex: 21332 ECONCOM-CE, Cable: ECONCOM, COLOMBOFax: 94-11-2329795

BOARD OF INVESTMENT OF SRI LANKA

Based on the above, the BOI by its letter dated 29.03.2002, grantedapproval to the company to undertake lecture course “pre-clinicalpart” of medical degrees to be offered by a foreign university.

Accordingly, the agreement with the BOI was signed on 18.07.2002.However, it is reported that the project was not implemented due to acase filed by Medical College against this company which has nowbeen concluded as informed by Vignan Educational Foundation (Pvt)Ltd. Having concluded the case, the company has commenced therecruting of students for their courses.

ÀåÚÈèï¾àºëÉ22712272

After the recent protest made by the undergraduates, the BOI by itsletter dated 10.11.2006 suspended the institution in conducting lecturecourses for the medical degree to be offered by the foreign universityin Tanzania.

Thereafter, by letter dated 15.11.2006, the BOI has requested thecompany to provide documentary evidence for the following in orderto consider the lifting of the suspension:

*Approval from the University Grants Commission*Approval from the Medical Council*Approval from the Ministry of Higher Education*Affiliation agreement signed with International Medical andTechnological University for medical degrees to be conferred*Approval from the Ministry of Health to undertake the LectureCourses

Forwarded for your information please.

Yours faithfully,A.M.C.KulasekaraDEPUTY DIRECTOR GENERAL (INVESTMENT)BOARD OF INVESTMENT OF SRI LANKA

SRI LANKA MEDICAL COUNCIL31, NORRIS CANAL ROAD, COLOMBO - 10In reply please quote MCI2006.11.23

C. A. Appln. No. 955/2003

Before: Chandra Ekanayake, J. andS. Sriskandarajah, J.

Counsel: Romesh de Silva, P. C., for Petitioners.Shibley Aziz, P. C., for Respondent.

Argued &Decided on: 26.04.2006

Chandra Ekanayake, J.

The respondent agrees;

(1) that the Respondent will not proceed on the paper advertisementsmarked P14 A to P14E or any of them and further undertakesthat it will not state in any public forum that it will not recongnisethe Pre Clinical Course conducted by the petitioners in Sri Lanka.

(2) that the aforesaid is without prejudice to its rights in terms of thelaw.

In view of the above these proceedings are terminated. No costs.

JUDGE OF THE COURT OF APPEAL

S. Sriskandarajah, J.I agree.

JUDGE OF THE COURT OF APPEAL

ªÇæ Ç ¨Çæ¸å¾åÆ¨ ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ¼ ¯ÝµÇ·Ç»¯Æ¯)(The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake)Thank you, Mr. Deputy Speaker, for giving me theopportunity to present the following Adjournment Motion.

“Today the aviation industry is not only turbulent but verycompetitive and profitability is a big question mark. SriLankan Airlineswas privatized by the People’s Alliance administration on the 30thMarch 1998. With that today the 10 year exclusive period is comingto an end on the 30th of March 2008. The Government has notconfirmed the way forward for SriLankan Airlines. In the meanwhilewe are informed that second budget airline in the name of “MihinAir” has been incorporated. Is this with state funds? If so, is thiswith Cabinet approval? And if not, how has the Governmentexpenditure been expended without Cabinet approval. Would theMinister of Aviation please inform this House on that and aviationpolicy that is being implemented at this moment”.

The Adjournment Motion deals on the aviation policyof Sri Lanka, especially on “Mihin Air” that has beenimplemented as of today. Hon. Minister, you being a veryresponsible and an active Minister, once again I would liketo see the activeness that would come up with some of thepertinent questions that come up for public probity.

Today, as you know the Government’s aviation policyhas yet to be spelt out properly, because this is an industrythat is very, very turbulent. Owing to the external factorssuch as the fuel prices going up et cetera, today the aviationindustry is in the doldrums. We are worried as to how itsfuture is going to be.

On that basis the “open skies” policy is something whichthe Government has to spell out very emphatically. It hasgot to say whether it is “open skies”, whether it is open tosome and closed to the others or whether it is for the purposeof a restricted basis. In today’s competitive world “openskies” is obviously the answers to this and what we arelooking forward to is, as to what Sri Lanka’s “open skies”policy would be. In this context, today you are talking ofa new budget airline that is supposed to have beenincorporated. I would like to know the answers to certainquestions which I will be asking.

In 1979 we had Air Lanka. This was set up with thetakeover of Air Ceylon which was running at that particularmoment in an inefficient, haphazard and lethargic manner.

2006 ï¾åÉæÂÚ 3022892290

From 1979 to 1998 Air Lanka was flying the National Flagof the country. Then, they decided to sell 40 per cent ofits shares. The reason being, the profitability and theefficacy was in question and there was a decision to privatizeit. Whether it was privatized in the right manner or not, isnot the question at this particular moment. It is still goingon. Then what happened was, owing to the fact that 40 percent of its shares were sold, a ten-year exclusive periodwas given for Emirates to manage it. This was simplybecause we felt that we did not have the proper managementto do so.

Going on further, with enormous amounts of money thatstill needs to be collected, the Government has only 15months more before the exclusive period comes to an end.The exclusivity given to Emirates Airline will come to anend on the 30th of March, 2008. So, we want to knowwhether the Hon. Minister or any entity has decided tonegotiate with them further or is it going to come back tothe Sri Lankan Government on the basis that there is noprivatization - [Interruption.] That will be 2008. ºÉºà¡ÉêÇæ¼à¼¨à ºøïÂ¾Éå ÄÍå®åÚÆºëÄå. Then, on the other side, if itis not being discussed or if it is being discussed, then, haveyou accepted privatization as a panacea for certain ills thatare there and is that one of the reasons for going forward?

The next one is, even if you decide not to negotiate orto negotiate, the very aspect of talking of a new airlinecoming up such as Mihin Air, only devalues the ultimateprice that you could get from anybody if you intendprivatizing or with Emirates et cetera. So, we would liketo have an answer from the Government on that score.Further, we are going on the hypothesis that there is the“open skies” policy. The private sector has been told tocome and operate as freely as they could. Tourism-ledeconomic growth is what is being looked at for Sri Lanka.You have private companies such as Expo Air, Holiday Air,Deccan Air that have got Government approval to flyinternationally.

ªÇæ ÄâªÈ ÌÄÇÑÇ ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ º+Æ¯¿ ±º¼¼)(The Hon. Mangala Samaraweera)No, I think, we are getting into another area of debatewhether privatization is correct or not. As for the second issue raised by the Hon. RaviKarunanayake and the Hon. Anura Dissanayaka, first of all,let me say that our Government believes that theintroduction of budget airline services in Sri Lanka inkeeping with international trends at the moment will be ofgreat benefit to air travel consumers of our country. Ofcourse, we must ensure that the safety and sustainability ofsuch operations are in order.

Of course, as for the subsequent questions which wereraised. So far, no Cabinet Paper has yet been presented butI believe in the next few weeks a joint Cabinet Paper willbe prepared by the Ministry of Finance along with theMinistry of Ports and Aviation which will givecomprehensive details regarding the formation of such abudget airline venture. But, for the moment I cannot giveyou any more details because no Cabinet Paper so far hasbeen presented by my ministry or any other ministry but asI said, most probably, it will be done in the next week orso. ¾øïÆåà¯ñ ¨»å¾åÆ¨ºëÄå(¼¶È±Æ ±¹Ç·Ç»¯¼Æ £Á¼Æ¯¿Æ)(The Deputy Speaker)¾øÊàÊ¼ É¾à¾. ÌÃåï ¨´Æêºë ºÉ ¾å ¨ùÀÆ¨à ¢¼úÖÆ´ ïª¾ÆçÄ´ ÌÃåï ¦¨­ºåÉÆ ºøïÂ¾Éå¼?

Once the Cabinet approval is granted for this project, ofcourse, there are certain procedures we will have to follow.As you know the application at that particular point in timewill be processed by the Civil Aviation Authority and inthat process we will give priority to ensure that thisapplication is in accordance with the air navigationregulation and the applicable international standards andrecommended practices which is basically the bible of theInternational Civil Aviation Organization. So, all thoseprocedures will be followed. All I can assure you, the Hon.Members and this House, is that the safety and the securitywill never be compromised in processing such applications.

Subscription : The annual subscription for Official Report of Hansard is Rs. 2,178. A single copy of Hansard is available forRs. 18.15. (Postage Rs. 2.50) Copies can be obtained by remitting in advance an annual subscription fee to theSUPERINTENDENT, GOVERNMENT PUBLICATION BUREAU, No. 32, Transworks House,Lotus Road, Colombo 1. The fee should reach him on or bvefore November 30 each year.Late application for subscriptions will not be accepted.
